<div id="review_1307105644" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307105644" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1307105644?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471115486" href="/book/show/25443389-extraordinary-means">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=simon-and-schuster-australia">simon-and-schuster-australia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307105644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2893397006349930157">This review appears on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2015/07/06/extraordinary-means-by-robyn-schneider-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br/><br/>This is a sad book. Not because of the writing, but because of the subject matter. One kid with tuberculosis is sad enough, but you’ve got a whole facility filled when them in Extraordinary Means. This is not the type of book you’d pick up if you’re feeling down, but for those who can accept it, it offers an interesting concept for kids who just want to find themselves.<br/><br/>With total drug resistant TB, these kids have been quara</span>
  <span id="freeText2893397006349930157" style="display:none">This review appears on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2015/07/06/extraordinary-means-by-robyn-schneider-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br /><br />This is a sad book. Not because of the writing, but because of the subject matter. One kid with tuberculosis is sad enough, but you’ve got a whole facility filled when them in Extraordinary Means. This is not the type of book you’d pick up if you’re feeling down, but for those who can accept it, it offers an interesting concept for kids who just want to find themselves.<br /><br />With total drug resistant TB, these kids have been quarantined from the rest of the world until a cure is discovered. Sadie chooses to live her life with a resigned reluctance and internalised anger. Lane lives with ambition and hope for the future. I’m glad these two were able to make a difference in each other’s lives, but at the end of the day, you never know how long it’s going to be.<br /><br />I enjoyed Lane’s point of view, it felt authentic and honest, with his reluctance to accept that he’s sick and throwing everything into his studies for college. But his fixation on the future has taken away his ability to focus on the present, which is something that Sadie pulls out of him. Sadie is like his bright light, and together they are really sweet.<br /><br />Sadie was a character I had difficulty warming to. She’s dry, sarcastic and holds grudges against people who hurt her. She’s quite bitchy and cold towards Lane at first because of a misunderstanding she had in the past, but thankfully she gets better as the book goes on. I could see how she had resigned herself to her fate, was therefore rebellious and really didn’t care about consequences, even if she managed to hurt others in the process. But that doesn’t mean she isn’t realistic.<br /><br />With Robyn Schneiders amazing characterisation and snarktastic writing, why only three stars? Let me explain.<br /><br />So these teenagers are cooped up in a facility right, where they’re fed healthy food, are cut off from the world and are half-heartedly going to school. What do they do with themselves? Aside from hacking into the internet and the odd movie night here and there, Sadie and her friends make fun for themselves.<br /><br />And this is the conflict that I can’t get my head around. These highly contagious kids, sneak out of the facility and go to town. They go to Starbucks, they hang around the park, and they visit shops and interact with people. They don’t have just any illness, they have an incurable disease. This is how the zombie apocalypse starts people, a bunch of stupid infected people sneaking out and putting the entire population at risk from a worldwide epidemic because they couldn’t pull their heads together. And of course, because they’ve snuck out once and gotten away with it, they’re going to keep and doing it again and again.<br /><br />I can’t think of anything more horrifying than that.<br /><br />But on the other hand, you have to feel for these kids. They feel fine, and they don’t think it’s a big deal. They just want to have a normal life, no more medical bands, no more getting treated like kid gloves, no more doctor’s appointments and check ups.<br /><br />Yeah that’s why you have a facility with relative freedom to do whatever you want.<br /><br />The author’s note opened my mind on the topic. It gave me a wider appreciation for the author’s background and passion in writing from the perspective of people with diseases. But we have My Sister’s Keeper, The Fault in Our Stars, just not a YA book about TB. I guess it raised awareness about this silent disease of the young.<br /><br />Despite my earlier ranting, I enjoyed Extraordinary Means, I really did. Robyn Schneider has a knack for writing really real characters, whether they’re likable or not. Her humour and ease of writing is fantastic. But because of the reasons stated above, this just wasn’t the book for me.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Simon and Schuster Australia for sending me this book for review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2893397006349930157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564510350p2/8563233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266269248?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471115486" href="/book/show/25443389-extraordinary-means">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266269248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11919876591961707533">Also reviewed on <a href='http://sophiereadsya.blogspot.com/2015/05/extraordinary-means-by-robyn-schneider.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sophie Reads YA</a><br/><br/>I received an Advance Reader Copy from the publisher via NetGalley. This is no way impacted in my view.<br/><br/>From the synopsis, it is recommended to those who enjoy John Green or Stephen Chbosky, and I could definitely see the connection with Green, not with Chbosky, which was good for me, as I really couldn't stand The Perks of Being a Wallflower.<br/><br/>This book was nothing like I was expecting, though, to be honest, I don't know much about it when I requested it. This was a</span>
  <span id="freeText11919876591961707533" style="display:none">Also reviewed on <a href="http://sophiereadsya.blogspot.com/2015/05/extraordinary-means-by-robyn-schneider.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Sophie Reads YA</a><br /><br />I received an Advance Reader Copy from the publisher via NetGalley. This is no way impacted in my view.<br /><br />From the synopsis, it is recommended to those who enjoy John Green or Stephen Chbosky, and I could definitely see the connection with Green, not with Chbosky, which was good for me, as I really couldn't stand The Perks of Being a Wallflower.<br /><br />This book was nothing like I was expecting, though, to be honest, I don't know much about it when I requested it. This was a total case of cover love. From my first impressions of the book, based on both the cover and the, albeit vague, synopsis, I thought Extraordinary Means would be about teens with some sort of lung problems, perhaps cancer. To some extent, this impression was true, but it was such an understatement. In Extraordinary Means, Tuberculosis (TB) has returned, with a strain that is 'Total Drug Resistant' (TDR). Lane and Sadie, the protagonists in the novel, as well as their friends, are suffering from TDR-TB, and are patients in Latham House, a sanatorium for teenagers suffering from this condition. As the TB is drug resistant, there is as much a chance of death as there is of full recovery.<br /><br />I really enjoyed that this book was dual POV, and that the two voices were really likeable. Both Lane and Sadie seemed like 'real' teenagers, you could see their suffering, and their happiness, and they weren't perfect in any respect. I especially liked the fact the they had known each other as children at a summer camp, and that the history between them was explained and not just glossed over. One problem I did have, though a really small one, was the romance. Yes, I was a fan of it (and I shipped the characters), but it felt sort of rushed, though I understand why it was rushed - they both could die at any day.<br /><br />The book, and particularly TB, seemed to be really well researched, and I think this is something that Schneider should be praised for. The whole situation with the numerous x-rays, medical wrist sensors, and the different medications mentioned all made it seem even more real, as if it could actually happen, or was happening. <br /><br />Overall, Extraordinary Means was unlike the usual YA Contemporaries that I read, and I really would recommend this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11919876591961707533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1238940990" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1238940990" />
    <a title="Justine (bookwormaniac)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28744450-justine-bookwormaniac"><img alt="Justine (bookwormaniac)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427511076p2/28744450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1238940990?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine (bookwormaniac)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine (bookwormaniac)" href="/user/show/28744450-justine-bookwormaniac">Justine (bookwormaniac)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28744450-justine-bookwormaniac?shelf=books-that-broke-my-heart-2015">books-that-broke-my-heart-2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1238940990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10213278654225668900">Yes, yes, and yes. Robyn Schneider kicked some asses again. Both Lane and Sadie have a good impact on the story. However, Lane, as a boy, doesn't really sound like a guy in some parts of the story. There are some parts that are quite unbelievable for a guy to do or say. Nevertheless, believe or not, when I was reading this book, I felt like I was on a train slowly closing in to another train. Then finally, boom! Train-wreck it is.<br/><br/><blockquote>"But that's the thing about odds. Roll a die twice, and you expect</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10213278654225668900" style="display:none">Yes, yes, and yes. Robyn Schneider kicked some asses again. Both Lane and Sadie have a good impact on the story. However, Lane, as a boy, doesn't really sound like a guy in some parts of the story. There are some parts that are quite unbelievable for a guy to do or say. Nevertheless, believe or not, when I was reading this book, I felt like I was on a train slowly closing in to another train. Then finally, boom! Train-wreck it is.<br /><br /><blockquote>"But that's the thing about odds. Roll a die twice, and you expect two different results. Except it doesn't work that way. You could roll the same side over and over again, the laws of the universe intact and unchanging with each turn.It's only when you consider the past that the odds change. That things become less and less likely."</blockquote><br /><br />Well, that quote above is incredible. I have no words for it. Every word of it was giving me feels. And, can you see the writing style? I have no complaints. It's simply beautiful. <br /><br />This is way incomparable to Robyn Schneider's other book, The Beginning of Everything. Extraordinary Means is something you can't forget that easily. Because: 1) The cover is super-duper nice. 2) The catch-phrase in the cover is catchy. 3) The ending. <br /><br />The main characters having a sense of rebellion is way too good to add in the story. And there is this one word that struck me the most in this book and made me laugh even though I shouldn't laugh at that part is 'potato'. Well, aren't words like that surprising to see?<br /><br />Not to mention that every part of this book is averagely realistic for me and I felt like diving in with them in Latham House. <br /><br /><blockquote>"My miracle wasn't a cure. It was a second chance. But second chances aren't forever. And even miracles have an expiration date."</blockquote><br /><br />Some parts just left me in awe. Some parts were just meh. And some parts just made me sad. And if you ever want to read this, read it. The cover isn't misleading.</span>

<div id="review_1266250296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1266250296" />
    <a title="Nicola" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8803703-nicola"><img alt="Nicola" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587222161p2/8803703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266250296?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola" href="/user/show/8803703-nicola">Nicola</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19778889-extraordinary-means">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8803703-nicola?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266250296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5655167099583390722">This is my first of Robyn Schneider's books and I really wasn't disappointed. It reminded me of <i>Looking for Alaska</i> but with the added element of having an incurable disease from <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>. Don't get me wrong, though, <i>Extraordinary Means</i> is not a copycat and has its own, separate, world to immerse yourself in.<br/><br/>The story begins with Lane's point of view. He is a straight A student who spends his life studying to keep his GPA up and working his way towards admission at an Ivy League col</span>
  <span id="freeText5655167099583390722" style="display:none">This is my first of Robyn Schneider's books and I really wasn't disappointed. It reminded me of <i>Looking for Alaska</i> but with the added element of having an incurable disease from <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>. Don't get me wrong, though, <i>Extraordinary Means</i> is not a copycat and has its own, separate, world to immerse yourself in.<br /><br />The story begins with Lane's point of view. He is a straight A student who spends his life studying to keep his GPA up and working his way towards admission at an Ivy League college. It is a major inconvenience for him to be sent to Latham House, a sanatorium for sick kids, to deal with his incurable strain of TB. Lane's character development was immense. He realises that by focusing so much of his time on school and the future, he has forgotten to <b>live</b>. He has missed out on so much <i>fun</i> and so many opportunities that he didn't think were important until it was too late. Seeing him start to live his life, even if it's a restricted life, was so nice to see. <br /><br />Our second point of view is in the form of Sadie. She has been at Latham House for over a year and is sort of drifting as she isn't getting any better or worse. She doesn't know when she'll get to go home but she is fitting in at Latham in a way that she never did at home. She is cool, has a great group of friends and is a sneaky rule-breaker. <br /><br />The romance in the book is between Sadie and Lane who actually met before at summer camp when they were thirteen. Sadie thinks that Lane is responsible for something bad that happened to her at camp but that is quickly resolved and they begin to fall for each other. I thought they were really cute together and having the two view points was great as we got an insight into both of their thoughts and feelings. Whilst loving their relationship I couldn't help but dread how things would turn out given that they are both suffering from TB (and the fact there are two view points for two people in a relationship is always suspicious!). I really couldn't help but hope for them at the same time though which I guess is one of the messages here: however dark things seem, there is always hope.<br /><br />This could have been extremely depressing but there is a lot of humour which lightens the story just enough whilst also keeping enough gloom for you to keep wondering what the outcome is going to be. It's a book about hope, second chances and living in the moment.<br /><br /><i>“There’s a difference between being dead and dying. We’re all dying. Some of us die for ninety years, and some of us die for nineteen. But each morning everyone on this planet wakes up one day closer to their death. Everyone. So living and dying are actually different words for the same thing, if you think about it.”</i><br /><br />---<br /><i>I received a copy of this book from the publishers via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. All reviews are also posted to my blog: <a href="http://nicolareadsya.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Nicola Reads YA</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5655167099583390722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="updateActionLinks">
        <a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link1266250296" title="Flag this review as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=1266250296&amp;resource_type=Review&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F23149128-extraordinary-means">flag</a>





      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1266250296'><a id="like_count_review_1266250296" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1266250296?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">11 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F23149128-extraordinary-means">Like</a></span>
&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a href="/review/show/1266250296?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">see review</a>

<div id="review_1086516446" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1086516446" />
    <a title="Miguel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17056059-miguel"><img alt="Miguel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514544377p2/17056059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1086516446?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miguel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miguel" href="/user/show/17056059-miguel">Miguel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17056059-miguel?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17056059-miguel?shelf=2015-favorites">2015-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17056059-miguel?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17056059-miguel?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17056059-miguel?shelf=im-a-mess-right-now">im-a-mess-right-now</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1086516446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer680120373894528846"><a href='https://thequirkyreader.wordpress.com/2015/05/21/extraordinary-means-by-robyn-schneider/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Also posted at The Quirky Reader</a><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <em>“There’s a specific energy to different moments, and once you lose it, it can’t be recaptured. You’ve got to record it, or you’ve got nothing.”</em>
</blockquote>If <em>The Beginning of Everything </em>was the appetizer to my favorite meal then this book is the main course. I’ve always known that Robyn Schneider’s going to be one of those authors that, once you see their book in a bookstore, you’ll grab it without hesitation.<br/><br/><em>Extraordinary Means </em>is nothing new I’ve read in YA literature. </span>
  <span id="freeText680120373894528846" style="display:none"><a href="https://thequirkyreader.wordpress.com/2015/05/21/extraordinary-means-by-robyn-schneider/" rel="nofollow noopener">Also posted at The Quirky Reader</a><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“There’s a specific energy to different moments, and once you lose it, it can’t be recaptured. You’ve got to record it, or you’ve got nothing.”</em>
</blockquote>If <em>The Beginning of Everything </em>was the appetizer to my favorite meal then this book is the main course. I’ve always known that Robyn Schneider’s going to be one of those authors that, once you see their book in a bookstore, you’ll grab it without hesitation.<br /><br /><em>Extraordinary Means </em>is nothing new I’ve read in YA literature. I’m almost tempted to say that this is the sister companion of <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em>, under different circumstances, of course. I don’t want to give anything away other than my hopes of fueling your excitement for this wonderful novel.<br /><br />The story follows Lane and Sadie who unexpectedly reunite from summer camp to the TB sanatorium Latham House. They are joined with a wonderful cast of quirky (I know) characters: Nick, Marina, and Charlie. They’re squad is notoriously known for breaking some of Latham’s rules (like smuggling goods from the outside world) and being happy not miserable.<br /><br />I mentioned this before that what makes a good book for me is an amazing protagonist. In this case, Schneider crafted these two extraordinary protagonists. Lane and Sadie weren’t cardboard cutouts; they made me feel with them. I felt their doubts, their miseries, and their happiness. And that can be dangerous sometimes for a reader, when we get attached to a character but I don’t care. I AM GOING DOWN WITH THIS SHIP AND ITS CREW.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>“So that’s how you live a really great life. You make sure you have enough good days that you want to go back to.”</em>
</blockquote>If I were to describe this book, it would be uplifting contrary to the seemingly bleak synopsis it has. I don’t want to give anything away about the events of this book, but all you have to know is that this was an exhilarating journey for me. It was like a peaceful and warm summer night.<br /><br />Robyn Schneider is a godsend to the YA universe. I can’t imagine her books not existing. That’s why I’m pushing you and everybody else reading this review to check this woman’s work. Believe me when I say this: her words are extraordinary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="680120373894528846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2978520786512449850" style="display:none">ALRIGHT HERE WE GO Y'ALL THIS IS GOING TO BE AN ANGRY AND SEMI-COHERENT REVIEW RIDDLED WITH GIFS AND SPOILERS (which will be marked you can read this even if you're planning on reading this book--but honestly do you not value my opinion at all?!)<br><br>ugh!!! i had such high hopes for this book!<br><br>but, no. just like the love between two archetype'd robyn schneider characters, my beliefs were scorned. it was just <i>the beginning of everything: maybe we'll die how sad is that let's be pretentious we're so young so full of life so much wasted potential edition</i>. some amazing unique special snowflake she-doesn't-know-she's-beautiful perfect specimen of a girl falls in luuuuuuv with a hot guy. a completely vanilla, absolutely no interesting qualities type.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431936833ra/14884763.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and the love is scorned in both books can you believe it oh my god it's the twist no one saw coming <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[except like, no. i predicted from the get-go that <s>mary sue</s> sadie would dieeee. and it would be so saaaad and change mr. vanilla's life forever. boo hoo. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>what a coinky-dink that in this group of five friends, the survival rate of the disease is four out of five. SOMEONE'S GOTTA DIE. well, two people in this case. but whatever.<br><br><b>i don't even know how to organize this review. so many things pissed me off.</b> I NEVER EVEN WRITE FULL REVIEWS. I SCRAWL THINGS.<br><br>but when i don't like a book, i usually have that feeling going in! and despite my strong dislike of the beginning of everything, i still thought i was going to like this book!<br><br>this is mainly due to the following reasons:<br>1) i only heard good things<br>2) the premise is pretty cool<br>3) alright, fine, the cover rocks.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429215868ra/14550869.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>so with my expectations in mind, let's set up the plotline. this is going to be like mildly detailed so if you still want to read the book you should probably skip this part. <s>I'M SORRY I KNOW I SAID THIS WOULD BE SAFE TO REAd</s><br><br>poor widdle lane has TB. except it's now inexplicably different. it's completely resistant to drugs, <s>and yet the mortality rate at a sanatorium where everyone has it is a mere 20%.</s> also it's EXTREMELY CONTAGIOUS!!! but omg why are my parents worried lol i'm fine also they only have a 10% chance of contracting it if they're in contact with me but they'll be fired if they "test positive for exposure" (wtf??)<br><br>so <b>the science here doesn't really check out.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391648214ra/8425433.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>anyway, lane arrives at this top-notch expensive sanatorium, granted opportunities anyone else with TB would literally kill for (and that's just in the US). and he hates it there.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419157112ra/13002530.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>maybe i'm not being fair. but this is an epidemic, possibly a pandemic, and his only symptoms are being tired once in a while and coughing sometimes, and this kid is chilling having amazing once-in-a-lifetime experiences with his perfectly quirky popular clique, who are just too cool to deal with these people trying to help them, and they could only ever possibly flourish in this obscure scenario. honestly i cannot picture these kids at a public high school.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397358992ra/9267403.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>SPEAKING OF WHICH, why are there only teenagers in this place?!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437431180ra/15585366.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>anyway he falls in with this group and then falls in love with unique beauty over there, blah blah blah. occasional insertion of coughing fit as a reminder that <b>This Typical And Boring Love Story Is Beautiful Because They Might Die</b>. how deep.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437430654ra/15585296.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>then more stuff happens and shit hits the fan but it's all right but then it's A MILLION TIMES WORSE.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437430654ra/15585297.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>except that at the page that probably inspired tears in some of people who cry during john green books, i cracked an incredulous grin.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408240846ra/10828447.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>don't waste your time on this book.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403887051ra/10158385.gif"   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yYNT29yLXcpWIc2thMVxggvJpvuomER9z3OmxehY0m6Qlkl6TW4eGd5k8qBviB+r0VLmqoJrEvaq9f/8kodWjA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

The revolt would be thwarted by a confluence of fierce weather and human betrayal, but Gabriel retained his dignity to the end. History knows little of Gabriel’s early life. But here, author Gigi Amateau imagines a childhood shaped by a mother’s devotion, a father’s passion for liberation, and a friendship with a white master’s son who later proved cowardly and cruel. She gives vibrant life to Gabriel’s love for his wife-to-be, Nanny, a slave woman whose freedom he worked tirelessly, and futilely, to buy. Interwoven with original documents, this poignant, illuminating novel gives a personal face to a remarkable moment in history.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11661024643813555211\" href=\"#\" If she finds Trent’s, then in a way, she will still have a piece of him.\n\nRisking everything to get closure once and for all, Quinn goes outside the system to track down nineteen-year-old Colton Thomas, whose life has been forever changed by this priceless gift. <span id="freeTextContainer5838359310716733802">Robyn Schneider is the bestselling author of The Beginning of Everything and Extraordinary Means, which have earned numerous starred reviews, appear on many state reading lists, and are published in over a dozen countries. Her next book, Invisible Ghosts, comes out in June from Katherine Tegen Books/HarperCollins. Robyn is a graduate of Columbia University, where she studied creative writing, and </span>
  <span id="freeText5838359310716733802" style="display:none">Robyn Schneider is the bestselling author of The Beginning of Everything and Extraordinary Means, which have earned numerous starred reviews, appear on many state reading lists, and are published in over a dozen countries. Her next book, Invisible Ghosts, comes out in June from Katherine Tegen Books/HarperCollins. Robyn is a graduate of Columbia University, where she studied creative writing, and the University of Pennsylvania Perelman School of Medicine, where she earned a Masters of Bioethics. She lives in Los Angeles, California, but also on the internet.</span>
